<span id="freeTextContainer672492184507711853">There are some books when you finish, you just sit motionless with blank face, feeling speechless, resuming your awkward position for hours and then you turn back into your life after getting frozen by a magical dramatic literary wand’s power. That’s what happened to me. And I realized I haven’t written any word about this stunning, amazing book and now Witherspoon and Washington’s Hulu series is streaming right now and it seems like scriptwriter Liz Tigelaar caught the essence of the plot and r</span>
  <span id="freeText672492184507711853" style="display:none">There are some books when you finish, you just sit motionless with blank face, feeling speechless, resuming your awkward position for hours and then you turn back into your life after getting frozen by a magical dramatic literary wand’s power. That’s what happened to me. And I realized I haven’t written any word about this stunning, amazing book and now Witherspoon and Washington’s Hulu series is streaming right now and it seems like scriptwriter Liz Tigelaar caught the essence of the plot and reflected into 8 great episodes (especially episode 7 was remarkably the best and heartfelt one) And Witherspoon’s Elena is her best book character composition. I highly recommend it! (Better than Big Little Lies)<br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1581834202i/28971646._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br> So here we go: this book is character driven, slow burn drama which will help a lot turn into series to give us so much details and realistic portraits about characters, always works well for me. Small town dynamics, dysfunctional family issues, class differences, morality about a child’s own destiny, hypocrisy, lies, secrets mixing each other and slow-building tension rises at the end with powerful, thought- provoking, twisty ending leaves you speechless.<br><br> Welcome to Shaker Heights! Richardson household is burning into fire and their daughter Izzy is nowhere to be seen. She might be responsible of this chaos. Then we slowly going back and forth between the snippets of Richardson family’s relationship with poor artist Mia and her daughter Pearl who became their tenants and afterwards.<br><br> And behind their story, there is custody war over a Chinese baby’s adoption by Richardson family’s close friends. Should baby be adopted by people who are so rich and ready to present her every opportunity she’s dreamed of or should her biological mother take the custody even though they may suffer from poorness and financial struggles?<br><br> Unhealthy, ballistic relationship with Izzy and her mother and striking differences between Mia and Elena and too many lies and secrets’ revelations change everything in their lives. When the fire starts to destroy everything they had in their lives, they need to start from scratch and learn from their mistakes.<br><br> It’s powerful, emotional, questioning, unique story. I know it’s so challenging to pick a side because nobody is blameless and innocent. I hope we see a good adaption without losing the essence of the story and its well-crafted characterization.<br><br><a href="https://niluferozmekik.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">blog</a><br><a href="https://www.instagram.com/nilylovestoread/" rel="nofollow noopener">instagram</a><br><a href="https://www.facebook.com/nilufer.ozmekik" rel="nofollow noopener">facebook</a><br><a href="https://twitter.com/NiluferOzmekik" rel="nofollow noopener">twitter</a></span>

<div id="review_1772984405" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1772984405" />
    <a title="Maxwell" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1381728-maxwell"><img alt="Maxwell" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1539318702p2/1381728.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1772984405?book_show_action=true">Oct 01, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Maxwell" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Maxwell" href="/user/show/1381728-maxwell">Maxwell</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780525522560" href="/book/show/36232831-little-fires-everywhere">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1381728-maxwell?shelf=owned">owned</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1381728-maxwell?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1772984405" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3295945499967965090">When I read Celeste Ng's debut novel <a>
  <i>Everything I Never Told You</i>
</a> in late 2014, I was smitten. Ng's writing was so beautiful, her characters so real, and the story so compelling. I instantly knew I would be reading whatever she put out next.<br/><br/>Three years later and I'm happy to say that Ng has returned with <i>just</i> as stunning of a novel as her debut. <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/34273236.Little_Fires_Everywhere' title='Little Fires Everywhere by Celeste Ng' rel='nofollow noopener'>Little Fires Everywhere</a> is hands down one of the best books I've read this year; and just like its predecessor will be rising to the top of my yearly</span>
  <span id="freeText3295945499967965090" style="display:none">When I read Celeste Ng's debut novel <a>
  <i>Everything I Never Told You</i>
</a> in late 2014, I was smitten. Ng's writing was so beautiful, her characters so real, and the story so compelling. I instantly knew I would be reading whatever she put out next.<br /><br />Three years later and I'm happy to say that Ng has returned with <i>just</i> as stunning of a novel as her debut. <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/34273236.Little_Fires_Everywhere" title="Little Fires Everywhere by Celeste Ng" rel="nofollow noopener">Little Fires Everywhere</a> is hands down one of the best books I've read this year; and just like its predecessor will be rising to the top of my yearly favorites list.<br /><br />I don't want to say too much about this novel because with Ng's books, I've discovered, it's best to go in anticipating very little and being surprised along the way. Because she is <b>very</b> good at surprises—and not the kind of plot twists you'll read in a thriller or spy novel; the kind of surprises that sneak up on you in real life and seem to tear your world apart. Her novels are domestic, but they aren't quaint. They have a raw, emotional power to them that are especially drawn out by her incredibly crafted characters. The inner turmoil is just as important as the external conflict in her stories, and that makes for a compulsively readable, yet immensely relatable read. You can empathize with so many parties in her stories, and this one is no exception. <br /><br />To me, these characters jumped from the pages; they have the mannerism (she's <i>so</i> observant, akin to Adichie in that sense) and the motivations of people you know in your own life. Mrs. Richardson's ethics and worldview are as real and as contrary as Mia's artistic sentiments. And you can't help feeling for both of them at times. That's what makes this story so good—there is no black and white, despite the obviously drawn lines between the differing characters. Ng exists in the grey, and her mission, it seems to me, is to pull you in to the grey too and think about how murky and complicated and messy life is.<br /><br />I'll stop gushing, but only as long as people go pick this up and read it (along with her first novel too)! Ng is surely one of my favorite living writers, and, again, I can't wait to see what she does next.</span>
  <a data-text-id="3295945499967965090" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2484708983" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2484708983" />
    <a title="jessica" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/10171516-jessica"><img alt="jessica" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1509983330p2/10171516.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2484708983?book_show_action=true">Aug 22, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="jessica" class="user" itemprop="url" name="jessica" href="/user/show/10171516-jessica">jessica</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780349142920" href="/book/show/36509779-little-fires-everywhere">review of another edition</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2484708983" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8316435191090393936"><b>
  <i>‘all her life, she had learned that passion, like fire, was a dangerous thing. it so easily went out of control.’</i>
</b><br/><br/>i honestly wasnt expecting to enjoy this book. i didnt really like celeste ngs debut and i thought this was probably overhyped. but this is one of the few occasions where i am actually happy to admit i was wrong. <br/><br/>i knew from the first chapter, where the title comes into play, that i was in for a real treat. if you dont know by now, i love when a book is so aptly named. sometimes t</span>
  <span id="freeText8316435191090393936" style="display:none"><b>
  <i>‘all her life, she had learned that passion, like fire, was a dangerous thing. it so easily went out of control.’</i>
</b><br /><br />i honestly wasnt expecting to enjoy this book. i didnt really like celeste ngs debut and i thought this was probably overhyped. but this is one of the few occasions where i am actually happy to admit i was wrong. <br /><br />i knew from the first chapter, where the title comes into play, that i was in for a real treat. if you dont know by now, i love when a book is so aptly named. sometimes titles can come across as lazy or appear as an afterthought, so there is nothing i love more than when a title is given some meaning and depth. and this book does that perfectly. <br /><br />i love how this book explores so many themes - such as motherhood, race, friendship, community, children - each one a little fire that slowly burned into an explosion of a story. i think ng is so clever in how she likens so many topics to a fire, bright with a burning intensity and heat. but with fire and scorched earth can come new beginnings. izzys character is definitely the highlight for me. i loved seeing her come to accept this idea and burn her own way, blazing a path of her own choosing. <br /><br />i know this wont be a book for everyone due to its slow pace and prominent focus on character histories, but there is definitely a reason this book is so highly rated. and i am very relieved that i enjoyed such a great work of fiction.<br /><br /><b>↠ <i>4.5 stars</i></b></span>
  <a data-text-id="8316435191090393936" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4514828-susanne-strong?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4514828-susanne-strong?shelf=favorite-authors">favorite-authors</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4514828-susanne-strong?shelf=must-read">must-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4514828-susanne-strong?shelf=traveling-sister-read">traveling-sister-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4514828-susanne-strong?shelf=edelweiss">edelweiss</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4514828-susanne-strong?shelf=2017-five-star-books">2017-five-star-books</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1996555816" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16870173095606589608"><b>5 Amazing Bright Shiny Stars! I would give it 100 if Goodreads would let me. <br/><br/>Little Fires Everywhere is a novel that far surpasses any other that I have ever read. </b> I don't know how Celeste Ng did it. It is a brilliantly written novel with intricate, rich and wholly vivid characters whose lives are so fully intertwined you can't help but read on in bewildered awe of how Celeste Ng created these characters. My nerve endings were fully engaged on high alert from the first sentence.<br/><br/>Shaker Heights, </span>
  <span id="freeText16870173095606589608" style="display:none"><b>5 Amazing Bright Shiny Stars! I would give it 100 if Goodreads would let me. <br /><br />Little Fires Everywhere is a novel that far surpasses any other that I have ever read. </b> I don't know how Celeste Ng did it. It is a brilliantly written novel with intricate, rich and wholly vivid characters whose lives are so fully intertwined you can't help but read on in bewildered awe of how Celeste Ng created these characters. My nerve endings were fully engaged on high alert from the first sentence.<br /><br />Shaker Heights, Ohio is an affluent town with rules and regulations like no other. Mrs. Richardson lives by them, having been raised by them and she has raised her four children (Lexie, Trip, Moody and Izzy) to abide by them as well. She rents a little apartment in Shaker Heights to Mia Warren and her daughter Pearl, who are less fortunate. Mia is a free spirited artist, who lives life to the fullest. These women have one thing in common and one thing only: they love their children immensely and they accept each other's as their own. Mia (or rather Ms. Ng) describes it beautifully: <br /><br /><blockquote>"To a parent, your child wasn't just a person, your child was a place, a kind of Narnia, a vast eternal place where the present you were living and the past you remembered and the future you longed for all existed at once. You could see it every time you looked at her; layered in her face was the baby she'd been and the child she'd become and the adult she would grow up to be and you saw them all simultaneously, like a 3-D image. It made your head spin. It was like a place you could take refuge, if you knew how to get in. And each time you left it, each time your child passed out of your sight, you feared you might never be able to return to that place again." </blockquote><br /><br />Neither live perfect lives, sometimes in fact they make grave mistakes, yet their love for their children never falters. <br /><br />These mothers relationships with each other, their family and everyone in town is threatened when a custody battle ensues between a friend of the Richardsons, Mrs. and Mr. McCullough, who are in the middle of adopting a Chinese American baby and a friend of Mia's, Bebe, who is the birth mother. This battle wrecks havoc on the town and causes incredible strife between the families. <br /><br /><b>This novel is captivating and crazy compelling. These characters burn an indelible image onto your soul. </b> The character of Izzy, Mrs. Richardson's daughter had me from the beginning (kind of like Hannah from Ms. Ng's Everything I Never Told You - which I also loved). Izzy has a strength and over came odds that most children in her position wouldn't. Her triumphs made my heart soar. <br /><br />Somehow Ms. Ng made me change my mind about some of the characters throughout the course of this novel. <b>In the beginning, I felt one way about two of the characters and then by the end, I did a complete switcheroo, and my feelings about them were FIERCE. </b><br /><br /><b>Little Fires everywhere brought forth laughter and lots of tears. It is that kind of novel. I can't recommend it highly enough. It is captivating, compelling and full of heart and soul. Celeste Ng's ability to intertwine the characters and storylines was wondrous, brilliant and beautiful. I loved every second of this book. <u> It has now topped my list as my FAVORITE BOOK of ALL TIME. </u></b><br /><br />Little Fires Everywhere was a Traveling Sister Group Read and included Brenda, Norma, Jennifer, Holly, Melissa &amp; Kendall. We all had a fabulous time reading this one together - the group discussions for this incredible read were amazing and I look forward to our next read together. <br /><br />For the full Traveling Sisters Group Review, please see Norma and Brenda's Blog:<br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://www.twogirlslostinacouleereading.wordpress.com/">https://www.twogirlslostinacouleeread...</a><br /><br />Thank you to Edelweiss, Penguin Press and Celeste Ng for an ARC of this novel in exchange for an honest review.<br /><br />Published on Goodreads, Edelweiss and Amazon on 9.17.17.</span>
  <a data-text-id="16870173095606589608" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780735224292" href="/book/show/34273236-little-fires-everywhere">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13427823-maureen?shelf=netgalley">netgalley</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2152158541" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12554909122810760240">Metaphorically speaking, everyone has 'little fires' in their lives - events that begin as a small spark, and have the ability to transform into a raging inferno, changing lives for ever.<br/><br/>Shaker Heights, Cleveland is an idyllic place to live, everything has been planned to create the perfect community, but it's residents are expected to live by its many rules and regulations.<br/><br/>The Richardson's are quintessentially the kind of family who the community of Shaker Heights was built for. Elena Richardso</span>
  <span id="freeText12554909122810760240" style="display:none">Metaphorically speaking, everyone has 'little fires' in their lives - events that begin as a small spark, and have the ability to transform into a raging inferno, changing lives for ever.<br /><br />Shaker Heights, Cleveland is an idyllic place to live, everything has been planned to create the perfect community, but it's residents are expected to live by its many rules and regulations.<br /><br />The Richardson's are quintessentially the kind of family who the community of Shaker Heights was built for. Elena Richardson was brought up with these rules, and she and her husband are determined that their four children, Lexie, Trip, Moody and Izzy will live by them too. Izzy isn't exactly a chip off the old block though, and will prove to be very disruptive.<br /><br />The Richardson's rent out an apartment to people they feel need a helping hand, and their latest tenants are Mia and her daughter Pearl. Mia is a free spirit, an artist specialising in photography, and when Elena’s troublesome daughter Izzy becomes close to Mia, Elena finds that she's jealous of the relationship, a relationship that doesn't exist between her and Izzy. Further to this, an adoption case in the community puts Elena and Mia on opposing sides, and Elena decides to do some digging on Mia’s past, and uproots some secrets that will change everything. <br /><br />Oh gosh, this book explores so many issues, but for me the one that stood out was motherhood, and in particular, the relationship between mothers and daughters, from baby's early days to teenage angst. <br /><br />It was beautifully written, with characters so well developed I felt as if I knew them personally. I also liked the setting of Shaker Heights, a place so perfect and orderly, and yet, ultimately there is always someone who will rip up those precious rules and regulations and throw them in the garbage. <br /><br />Celeste Ng writes with great insight and empathy, and leaves the reader with much to think about.<br /><br />*Thank you to Netgalley and Little, Brown Book Group for my ARC in exchange for an honest review*</span>

<div id="review_1904073279" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1904073279" />
    <a title="Angela M" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4685500-angela-m"><img alt="Angela M" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1512600770p2/4685500.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1904073279?book_show_action=true">Jun 26, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Angela M" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Angela M" href="/user/show/4685500-angela-m">Angela M</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780735224292" href="/book/show/34273236-little-fires-everywhere">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4685500-angela-m?shelf=edelweiss-reviews">edelweiss-reviews</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1904073279" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8557353364531488080"><br/>The Richardson family lives a perfect life, planned to a T and that's what Elena Richardson, her husband and four children seem to have, at least to fifteen year old Pearl Warren. Pearl moves with her itinerant artist mother, Mia, into a rental house owned by the Richardsons in Shaker Heights and becomes infatuated with this family, their house, their life style so different from her own and is mostly infatuated with three of the teenage siblings. The reader though knows from the get go that the</span>
  <span id="freeText8557353364531488080" style="display:none"><br />The Richardson family lives a perfect life, planned to a T and that's what Elena Richardson, her husband and four children seem to have, at least to fifteen year old Pearl Warren. Pearl moves with her itinerant artist mother, Mia, into a rental house owned by the Richardsons in Shaker Heights and becomes infatuated with this family, their house, their life style so different from her own and is mostly infatuated with three of the teenage siblings. The reader though knows from the get go that there's no perfection here . An awful thing happens to this family and we know what it is from the first sentence but I won't give it away. <br /><br />The Shaker Heights motto is: "Most communities just happen; the best are planned " : the underlying philosophy being that everything could - and should- be planned out, and that by doing so you could avoid the unseemly, the unpleasant, and the disastrous." The truth is that life happens and no matter what - things cannot be avoided and what happens here defies this underlying philosophy. <br /><br />But this is not the most awful thing that happens in this family. For me it was the dysfunctional relationship that Elena has with her youngest daughter Izzy . Izzy reminds me in some ways of Hannah in Ng's last book, Everything I Never Told You. Unlike Hannah, Izzy is not invisible not totally ignored, but she is picked on, made fun of and seems to always be the recipient of her mother's impatience with things that are not perfect. Theirs is not the only mother-daughter relationship that Ng focuses on . There is Mia and Pearl, who move from place to place, with Pearl not knowing the reason why or who her father was. There is Bebe, Mia's coworker, and her newborn baby May-Ling that she abandons and then fights to get custody. Bebe's story at first seems secondary but it ends up being the impetus for Elena's almost obsessive search to find out Mia's past. <br /><br />Ng delves deep into her characters and you feel you know them inside and out even though it takes until the end to fully understand Elena and Izzy. You may not like all of them but you will understand them . This I find to be Ng's strength as a writer- how she makes us know her characters. One of the most poignant scenes in the novel, is when the Richardsons find the photographs that Mia leaves for them. She came to know them too . Definitely recommended to those who were fans of Everything I Never Told You, and stories of families who are less than perfect, which I'm sure many of us can relate to. <br /><br /> I received an advanced copy of this book from Penguin Publishing Group through Edelweiss.<br />The book links are not working for me now but I'll try again later to insert them. </span>
  <a data-text-id="8557353364531488080" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  <div class="friendReviews elementListBrown" >
    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_2253720606" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2253720606" />
    <a title="Emily" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2431873-emily"><img alt="Emily" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1477433724p2/2431873.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2253720606?book_show_action=true">Feb 03, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Emily" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Emily" href="/user/show/2431873-emily">Emily</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780735224292" href="/book/show/34273236-little-fires-everywhere">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2431873-emily?shelf=literary-fiction">literary-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2431873-emily?shelf=book-club">book-club</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2253720606" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15664582598946843134">I really did not want to read this book. Unfortunately for me, it was a book club pick, so I read it in one sitting on a plane. I was grumpy for the first hundred pages, which I thought might have been unwarranted. Most of my initial ire went to this: what was the purpose of setting this so firmly in 1998?? Why does the book double down so much on referencing TLC, The Mighty Mighty Bosstones, the Clinton-Lewinsky scandal, Lexie's Explorer, and Charlie's Angels? (The date was confirmed for sure 2</span>
  <span id="freeText15664582598946843134" style="display:none">I really did not want to read this book. Unfortunately for me, it was a book club pick, so I read it in one sitting on a plane. I was grumpy for the first hundred pages, which I thought might have been unwarranted. Most of my initial ire went to this: what was the purpose of setting this so firmly in 1998?? Why does the book double down so much on referencing TLC, The Mighty Mighty Bosstones, the Clinton-Lewinsky scandal, Lexie's Explorer, and Charlie's Angels? (The date was confirmed for sure 254 pages into the book, when the date of May Ling's appearance at the fire station is stated as January 1997, but by then I was so oversaturated with Pearl using the dial-up internet in the library that I didn't care.) Maybe I am just being uncharitable, I thought, because I loved <i>Lady Bird</i>, a movie that is firmly set in 2002. Upon reflection, however, I have determined that the core difference between these two artistic attempts is that <i>Lady Bird</i> is actually good. This is not. <br /><br />This book sets up some interesting questions and themes around family, motherhood, and social conformity. The problem is that the author has a very clear answer to all of these questions, conveyed through very clumsy third-person narration. The third-person perspective switches between characters rapidly, just in time for them to have insights that seem out-of-place or too pat. Seventeen-year-old Trip Richardson, interested in girls and partying, thinks pensively that Pearl Warren "linger[s] comfortably in the grey spaces" between right and wrong. More egregiously, the family patriarch, Mr. Richardson, gets exactly one paragraph from his perspective, and it's this one:<br /><blockquote><i>He should have known better than to bring it up, he realized: it was too personal for her; she couldn't see clearly; she was so close that she didn't even realize how unclearly she was seeing ... But the problem with rules, he reflected, was that they implied a right way and a wrong way to do things. When, in fact, most of the time there were simply </i>ways<i>, none of them quite wrong or quite right, and nothing to tell you for sure which side of the line you stood on.</i></blockquote><br />It's one thing to set up this tension, between conformity and independence, and quite another to use a minor character as an authorial mouthpiece to hammer your point home so obviously. Do you not trust your story or your readers to do this work for you? <br /><br />The other big problem with the writing is that the author clearly favors Mia Warren, who is set up as a foil to Elena Richardson. Elena is a conforming suburban mother who downgraded her career to focus on her children, while Mia is a free-wheeling artist who not only knows how to live life outside the lines, but is (we are supposed to believe) a better mother than all of those repressed Shaker Heights mothers combined. I could not stand Mia Warren. If the author hadn't been so enamored with Mia, it's possible that I'd like her more; as it is, Mia <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[is a surrogate who runs away with the child, and then spends the rest of her life uprooting her teenage daughter's life every year to drive to a new place in the US <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>, which is TOTALLY CRAZY. I don't think the book understands how truly bananas this is and how far divorced from reality these plot points are: <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Mia, too poor to go to college, becomes a surrogate; her beloved mentor dies of a swift disease right as she could help; Mia is pregnant when her brother meets his untimely death and her parents are disgusted with her at the funeral; Mia runs away to San Francisco and proceeds to support herself on her art, without ever getting back in touch with her parents or having her parents try to find out where she is???? <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>. I almost sympathize with Elena Richardson, because I wanted to throttle Mia (and I didn't actually have to spend any time with her), but then I remember the incredibly ridiculous and poorly written scene in which Elena <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[breaks into the abortion records of a clinic, only to set off the subplot about her own daughter's abortion <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>.<br /><br />The one plot I found interesting was the story of May Ling/Mirabelle and her adoption, but this doesn't get very much page time. And again, this gets put through Mia's lens. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Mia ran away with her daughter when she had the chance; Bebe runs away with May Ling once the decision goes against her. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> I think the book could have worked better if at least one of the plot lines were removed to focus on this as a central conflict. <br /><br />Anyway, I'm a little surprised at how well this book is reviewed. I think you either have to really like slavish detail about Shaker Heights in 1998, or you have to enjoy reading a book where the author constantly moralizes at you. I fall into neither of those categories.</span>
  <a data-text-id="15664582598946843134" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2132882723" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2132882723" />

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30036082-warda?shelf=i-fell-in-love">i-fell-in-love</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30036082-warda?shelf=reread-worthy">reread-worthy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30036082-warda?shelf=author-of-colour">author-of-colour</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2132882723" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8193830915861239180">God, this was good. I’m speechless at this point of finishing the book. This story was pure magic. And to think I was about to unhaul it as well. The abomination. Can you imagine what I was about to miss out on?! <br/>Don’t worry, I kicked myself already!<br/><br/>Celeste Ng’s words are beyond captivating. She has, for me, created one of the best character driven stories ever. I’m not going to bother telling you what the plot is about. Go find out for yourself! You’re welcome! I’m serious, you are welcome!<br/><br/>As s</span>
  <span id="freeText8193830915861239180" style="display:none">God, this was good. I’m speechless at this point of finishing the book. This story was pure magic. And to think I was about to unhaul it as well. The abomination. Can you imagine what I was about to miss out on?! <br />Don’t worry, I kicked myself already!<br /><br />Celeste Ng’s words are beyond captivating. She has, for me, created one of the best character driven stories ever. I’m not going to bother telling you what the plot is about. Go find out for yourself! You’re welcome! I’m serious, you are welcome!<br /><br />As soon as I started reading, the writing drew me in. She is a master at letting the writing speak for itself. The mystery? It came from her writing. The intriguing plot? The writing. The conflict I was experiencing? The writing. The characters that I felt I knew to my core and actually existed for me? The flippin’ writing did it all. <br /><br />I kept on rereading a sentence because I felt that I could extract more meaning, more magic from it. I was relishing in it, holding it close for a while before I moved on to the next sentence and let it go. <br />But then I stumbled across one of those magical sentences again and the cycle started all over again. <br /><br />As for the characters, well, they were a treat. In the sense that if you enjoy reading characters that’ve been well-developed, that are layered, nuanced, flawed and realistic, this book is it for you. It was, essentially, a character study. You get to know them intimately and I enjoyed that aspect the most. These characters are not black and white. Each of them had their reasoning as to why they did what they did, the choices they made and the viewpoints they had. I loved this point was honed in time and time again; that circumstances shape who you are, who you become. That there are many different paths to living your life and that most of the time, things fall under the grey area. <br /><br />There were so many questions that were thrown at the reader and I liked that one had to think for oneself. The answers weren’t handed to you, because does life have all of the answers? You make choices and deal with the consequences, whether good or bad. It created for an interesting discussion and battle within my own head. <br /><br />One of my favourite books for sure. <br /><br />—————-<br /><br />Buddy-reading with <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/58818027-fares" rel="nofollow noopener">this gem of a human!</a><br /><br />This book has been receiving non-stop praise. You people better have not been lying about it.</span>

<div id="review_2064682058" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2064682058" />
    <a title="Liz" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4125660-liz"><img alt="Liz" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1316269997p2/4125660.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2064682058?book_show_action=true">Nov 14, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Liz" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Liz" href="/user/show/4125660-liz">Liz</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/34331079-little-fires-everywhere">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4125660-liz?shelf=book-clubs">book-clubs</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2064682058" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1585087138179804241">At first glance, this book seems to be mostly about teenagers, but then it struck me that it’s really about parenting. Each parent thinks they’re doing the right things in the way they raise their children. But who truly is? <br/><br/> Ng does a good job of bringing each character to life. Izzy is the most unique of the characters. And the relationship between Izzy and Mrs. Richardson is spot on perfect. “When it came to Izzy, Mrs. Richardson was seldom calm, and for that matter, Izzy herself never was.” </span>
  <span id="freeText1585087138179804241" style="display:none">At first glance, this book seems to be mostly about teenagers, but then it struck me that it’s really about parenting. Each parent thinks they’re doing the right things in the way they raise their children. But who truly is? <br /><br /> Ng does a good job of bringing each character to life. Izzy is the most unique of the characters. And the relationship between Izzy and Mrs. Richardson is spot on perfect. “When it came to Izzy, Mrs. Richardson was seldom calm, and for that matter, Izzy herself never was.” <br /><br />There are multiple storylines here, all equally fascinating. The one that grabbed me the most was between Bebe Chow and the McCulloughs. I flip flopped back and forth between whose side I was on. The heartache of both sides was palpable. <br /><br />It took a while for the book to truly grab me. But once it did, it really did. The title is so apt. Not just the physical fire, but the fires that burn within the characters, especially the fire that ignited in Mrs. Richardson. <br /><br />It’s interesting that the author refers to Mrs. Richardson by her formal name, whereas everyone else is called by their first name. It suits her perfectly, as she is such a stickler for tradition and following the rules. <br /><br />This is a fascinating book with a lot going for it. Five rich stars!<br /><br />Update - both of my book clubs had this as their selection this month. In both cases, the discussions were great. Any clubs looking for ideas, I highly recommend. </span>
  <a data-text-id="1585087138179804241" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="R.K. Gold" class="user" itemprop="url" name="R.K. Gold" href="/user/show/40737518-r-k-gold">R.K. Gold</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780735224292" href="/book/show/34273236-little-fires-everywhere">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2212249792" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11304085434501289888">I'd probably give this 3.5, I guess. I don't know. I didn't like this book, but I feel like I should. Ng is a phenomenal writer but I just couldn't get into this book. The first chapter was amazing and I thought I was in for something special.<br/><br/>There was a clear theme of ignorance in the "progressive" town of Shaker Heights that only outsiders and Izzy could see. The reason I couldn't get into this book was that all the supporting characters felt a little thin. Like they weren't actually people, t</span>
  <span id="freeText11304085434501289888" style="display:none">I'd probably give this 3.5, I guess. I don't know. I didn't like this book, but I feel like I should. Ng is a phenomenal writer but I just couldn't get into this book. The first chapter was amazing and I thought I was in for something special.<br /><br />There was a clear theme of ignorance in the "progressive" town of Shaker Heights that only outsiders and Izzy could see. The reason I couldn't get into this book was that all the supporting characters felt a little thin. Like they weren't actually people, they were just there to show how ignorant and selfish the people of Shaker Heights were.<br /><br />Mia was obviously a fantastic character and had multiple chapters dedicated to her backstory and why she became the artist she was/why she had the feelings about the central conflict that she had. By the end of the story it felt like there really wasn't a choice. Mia's side was clearly in the right and the Richardsons and the McCulloughs were too ignorant to ever really support. I don't know. I know there are people like them in the world. I know why this book is so popular and it deserves the success it's had.<br /><br />I just couldn't get into it.</span>
  <a data-text-id="11304085434501289888" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1973088950" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1973088950" />
    <a title="Meredith" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/30978160-meredith"><img alt="Meredith" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1423329725p2/30978160.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1973088950?book_show_action=true">Apr 16, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Meredith" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Meredith" href="/user/show/30978160-meredith">Meredith</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/34331079-little-fires-everywhere">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1973088950" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3234991545358000137"><b>
  <i>Intensely complex, multi layered, and intricately plotted Little Fires Everywhere is a profoundly complicated and jarring read about motherhood, freedom, and the human experience. </i>
</b><br/><br/>When unconventional artist Mia and her fifteen year old daughter, Pearl, move to Shaker Heights, Ohio their lives dramatically change. Of even great significance is their impact on the seemingly perfect Richardson family. On the surface, the Richardson’s seem to have it all--perfect house, perfect jobs, perfect chi</span>
  <span id="freeText3234991545358000137" style="display:none"><b>
  <i>Intensely complex, multi layered, and intricately plotted Little Fires Everywhere is a profoundly complicated and jarring read about motherhood, freedom, and the human experience. </i>
</b><br /><br />When unconventional artist Mia and her fifteen year old daughter, Pearl, move to Shaker Heights, Ohio their lives dramatically change. Of even great significance is their impact on the seemingly perfect Richardson family. On the surface, the Richardson’s seem to have it all--perfect house, perfect jobs, perfect children (minus one), but something is missing. Living in the bubble of the cookie cutter community of Shaker Heights, their world is insular and small. Mia and Pearl’s presence shakes them to the core and opens them up to a world of new possibilities. <br /><br />Told through the eyes of multiple characters, this is a slow burn read with fluid changes of POV. While one of the main events occurs in the first chapter, it isn't until the end that one can fully understand the implications of "the little fires everywhere."<br /><br />Here’s the thing--when I first started reading this, I had a hard time connecting to the characters and the plot. Several times I wanted to give up and start another book, but Ng’s beautiful writing kept pulling me back in. It wasn’t until about half way through, I felt the subtle spark of connection, and as it grew my feelings about this book grew. When I got to the end, I was simply stunned by how this book snuck up on me and overpowered my emotions. To sum up my reading experience: “And it was complicated, what had happened. It was a terribly awkward agonizingly slow, painfully intimate story that unfolded.” <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="3234991545358000137" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Diane S ☔" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Diane S ☔" href="/user/show/4159922-diane-s">Diane S ☔</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780735224292" href="/book/show/34273236-little-fires-everywhere">review of another edition</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1874607505" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer582111249230946575">An author that has the uncanny ability and insight to look deep inside the workings of the often complicated relationships between mothers and daughters. Mrs. Richardson prides herself on always following the rules, believing if this is done success in life and family will follow. She has four children , but as we know saying it doesn't make it so. Mia, a single mother, has a secret, a secret that will be used to her detriment. She was my favorite character, has a better, closer bond with her da</span>
  <span id="freeText582111249230946575" style="display:none">An author that has the uncanny ability and insight to look deep inside the workings of the often complicated relationships between mothers and daughters. Mrs. Richardson prides herself on always following the rules, believing if this is done success in life and family will follow. She has four children , but as we know saying it doesn't make it so. Mia, a single mother, has a secret, a secret that will be used to her detriment. She was my favorite character, has a better, closer bond with her daughter, Pearl, but mother's know, teenage daughter keep secrets too. A friend of Mrs Richardson, is unable to have children, but is given an opportunity that may not be hers to take.<br /><br />What an absolutely perfect title this was, small fires trailing these characters in their actions, words and the things they keep hidden. The way the story progresses, unravels, is brilliant, completely right. The different lifestyles, but always at heart is the question, "Nature vs. nurture, does lifestyle matter if the love is strong?" Unbreakable bonds, forged in many different ways. Sometimes by the time we have full realization of something important, it may be too late.<br /><br />This novel does something important, it makes one think, might make some open their eyes. Would be an excellent choice for a book group of woman. Much to discuss here.<br /><br />ARC from publisher.</span>

<div id="review_2122373867" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2122373867" />
    <a title="Julie " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5210022-julie"><img alt="Julie " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1356906542p2/5210022.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2122373867?book_show_action=true">Oct 11, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Julie " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Julie " href="/user/show/5210022-julie">Julie </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780735224292" href="/book/show/34273236-little-fires-everywhere">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5210022-julie?shelf=contemporary-fiction">contemporary-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5210022-julie?shelf=fiction-literature">fiction-literature</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5210022-julie?shelf=2017">2017</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5210022-julie?shelf=e-book">e-book</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5210022-julie?shelf=family">family</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5210022-julie?shelf=mothers-and-children">mothers-and-children</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5210022-julie?shelf=overdrive">overdrive</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2122373867" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15246401725151385727">Little Fires Everywhere by Celeste Ng is a 2017 Penguin Press publication. <br/><br/>A smart, but often scathing look at entitlement coupled with the endless dynamic layers between mother and child. <br/><br/><br/>The Clinton era gets a sharp examination as we drop in on Shaker Heights, an ideal suburban community with plenty of unspoken rules for its financially comfortable residents. The Richardson family is the prototype of the community, with Elena Richardson embracing the lifestyle with unparalleled enthusiasm. <br/><br/><b>‘Pe</b></span>
  <span id="freeText15246401725151385727" style="display:none">Little Fires Everywhere by Celeste Ng is a 2017 Penguin Press publication. <br /><br />A smart, but often scathing look at entitlement coupled with the endless dynamic layers between mother and child. <br /><br /><br />The Clinton era gets a sharp examination as we drop in on Shaker Heights, an ideal suburban community with plenty of unspoken rules for its financially comfortable residents. The Richardson family is the prototype of the community, with Elena Richardson embracing the lifestyle with unparalleled enthusiasm. <br /><br /><b>‘Perfection: that was the goal, and perhaps the Shakers had lived it so strongly it had seeped into the soil itself, feeding those who grew up there with a propensity to overachieve and a deep intolerance for flaws.’</b><br /><br />By contrast, Mrs. Richardson’s new tenants, Mia and her daughter, Pearl, live a free spirited, nomadic life. Mia is a photographer, who works just enough to afford the basics in life. Pearl, though, has no trouble adapting to the stable home life of the Richardson’s, practically becoming a member of the family. <br /><br />Things are working out well enough, until a chain of events unlocks long buried secrets, spawning a bitter custody battle, which exposes cracks in the Richardson’s perfect image, and will culminate in a fiery inferno, both physically and metaphorically. <br /><br />This second novel by Celeste Ng is not quite as grim or heavy as her debut, but it is every bit as provocative. <br /><br />I have had a hard time writing this review because the layers in this story are many, with so many themes to explore. I have worked on it for days, feeling slightly intimidated, unable to find the words that would do justice to such an outstanding novel. <br /><br />|<br /><br />This book adeptly explores hot button issues prevalent twenty years ago, between episodes of Jerry Springer and Clinton’s sex scandals, when a different set of questions were raised, such as interracial adoptions. <br /><br /><b>“It came, over and over, down to this: What made someone a mother? Was it biology alone, or was it love?”</b><br /><br />I was impressed with the various contrasts presented in the book, which included the mindset of the privileged juxtaposed against those who find themselves at their mercy. Was there an exacting price for that privilege and was it worth it? I must say, the judgmental hypocrisy is astounding!! <br /><br />But, the heartbeat of the story is centered around motherhood. Every mother represented exposed that instant vulnerability motherhood creates. The pain of infertility and the frustrating process of adoption is examined right along with parental sacrifices and foibles and their consequences. <br /><br />Mia and Mrs. Richardson's children also play an integral part in the story, their roles intertwined and connected in the most ironic of ways. <br /><br /><b>‘Izzy had the heart of a radical, but she had the experience of a fourteen-year-old in the suburban Midwest.’</b><br /><br /><br />One of the more interesting character studies is of Elena- mostly referred to as Mrs. Richardson, which I thought was a very clever way of hammering home a specific point. Her cluelessness, her arrogance, and relentless reproach is extraordinary in light of what is actually taking place.<br /><br />Mia, in turn, may spark a little resentfulness in Mrs. Richardson, and despite my initial puzzlement about her, and I admit I certainly questioned some of her choices, I ended up respecting her a great deal. <br /><br />So, as you can see, the novel is very driven by the characters, each offering a different perspective or new avenue in which to view the situation. Sometimes I felt deep empathy for one character, feeling the acuteness of their pain, but unable to choose a side. It is often heart wrenching and I found myself feeling torn on many occasions. <br /><br />On other occasions, I had a very hard time mustering up any real empathy for a few of these characters. <br /><br />The plotting was very tightly woven and on several occasions, I may have uttered an expletive out loud when misunderstandings exploded in the worst possible way, creating a mountain of tension in the process. <br /><br />This is a very compelling family drama, drawing out a bit of nostalgia, prompting me to take a closer look in the mirror, to put myself in the place of others before passing judgement. <br /><br />But, I also picked up on a bit of sarcasm here and there, almost as if the author was scoffing at some of the attitudes or the mindset of the era, although it was done so in an understated and sly way. <br /><br /><br />It’s been nearly a week since I finished the book and I still find myself mulling over the many layers and angles, and thinking about the characters and the choices they made and how it all came together in the end. <br /><br />So, it is fair to say, this book has had an impact on me, and think it is a novel anyone who appreciates a well written, thought provoking work of fiction will appreciate. Highly recommend!! <br /><br />5 stars <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="15246401725151385727" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_2214033636" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2214033636" />
    <a title="megs_bookrack" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/48328025-megs-bookrack"><img alt="megs_bookrack" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1532027727p2/48328025.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2214033636?book_show_action=true">Dec 20, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="megs_bookrack" class="user" itemprop="url" name="megs_bookrack" href="/user/show/48328025-megs-bookrack">megs_bookrack</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Audible Audio " href="/book/show/36112638-little-fires-everywhere">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2214033636" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18117343578252393217">The relationship between a mother and child <b>can be</b> a beautiful thing.<br/><br/>Let's be honest though, it's not always. <b>It can sometimes be messy, complex and immensely stressful</b> for both parties.<br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1545349904ra/26778834.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>In <i>Little Fires Everywhere</i>, Celeste Ng, weaves an intricate tapestry of such relationships. The resultant story is one of <b>family, loyalty, community and independence</b>. <br/><br/>When I went into this book, I thought it was a story about the adoption of a Chinese baby by a white family in suburban Ohio, showing the resulting</span>
  <span id="freeText18117343578252393217" style="display:none">The relationship between a mother and child <b>can be</b> a beautiful thing.<br><br>Let's be honest though, it's not always. <b>It can sometimes be messy, complex and immensely stressful</b> for both parties.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1545349904ra/26778834.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>In <i>Little Fires Everywhere</i>, Celeste Ng, weaves an intricate tapestry of such relationships. The resultant story is one of <b>family, loyalty, community and independence</b>. <br><br>When I went into this book, I thought it was a story about the adoption of a Chinese baby by a white family in suburban Ohio, showing the resulting community reactions and interactions based off that adoption. <br><br>While it is true that there is an adoption in the story, and the baby is in fact of Chinese descent, that is only a very small part of this deeply emotional tale.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1509213260ra/24301197.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Full disclosure, I never cried, but I was definitely moved. I was angry at times, sad and emotionally drained. <br><br>I had my curiosity peaked, my temper flare and most importantly, this story made me think about it even when I wasn't reading it. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1545350057ra/26778838.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I think that is a sign of a literary fiction novel doing its job; challenging the reader and causing them to think. <br><br>I had never read a Celeste Ng book before and was deeply impressed by her subtle way of drawing the reader into the emotions, drama and angst of her characters.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1504762686ra/23811972.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I must admit that Literary Fiction is not a genre I tend to gravitate towards. Like ever, but I am really glad that I went outside my comfort zone and picked this one up. <br><br>I think it helped that a significant portion of the story followed the perspective of teenagers, Pearl and the Richardson kids. I am not sure what that says about me, that I prefer that perspective, but there you go. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1573140273ra/28416859.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Overall, the varying perspectives really helped to complete the full narrative and I couldn't help but be totally engrossed in the lives of the Shaker Heights crew.<br><br>I definitely plan to read more of Ng's books in the future. Additionally, I did listen to the audiobook for this and thought that the narration was excellent!</span>
  <a data-text-id="18117343578252393217" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Tucker  (TuckerTheReader)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Tucker  (TuckerTheReader)" href="/user/show/70951605-tucker-tuckerthereader">Tucker  (TuckerTheReader)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2512266066" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5344905977372910344"><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1578606097i/28747601._SY540_.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>Soooo, Reese Witherspoon just added this to her book club thing? Which is so biased because SHE'S THE LEAD OF THE SHOW!<br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1555282220ra/27364209.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>***************<br/><br/>With Reese Witherspoon!!!!!<br/><br/>***************<br/><br/>YOU GUYS!! THEY'RE MAKING THIS A TV SHOW! FSHFGFKFJ!!!<br/><br/>***************<br/><br/>There is really no category to fit this book into. It's fiction but what kind? Contemporary? Kind of. Thriller? A bit. But not really. It's like the way a frosted sunrise (basically ice cream and orange juice blended to perfection.) tastes both sour and s</span>
  <span id="freeText5344905977372910344" style="display:none"><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1578606097i/28747601._SY540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Soooo, Reese Witherspoon just added this to her book club thing? Which is so biased because SHE'S THE LEAD OF THE SHOW!<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1555282220ra/27364209.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>***************<br><br>With Reese Witherspoon!!!!!<br><br>***************<br><br>YOU GUYS!! THEY'RE MAKING THIS A TV SHOW! FSHFGFKFJ!!!<br><br>***************<br><br>There is really no category to fit this book into. It's fiction but what kind? Contemporary? Kind of. Thriller? A bit. But not really. It's like the way a frosted sunrise (basically ice cream and orange juice blended to perfection.) tastes both sour and sweet all at the same time.<br><br>This book could never be a movie. I'm not saying that negatively. No, I would absolutely love to see this in the big screen but it's just written in such an amazing and unique way that only a book can portray. <br><br>This book is told in third person omniscient. This basically means it's told in he/she/they but from the POV of everyone. Kind of. It's almost like inside out where one moment were in one characters head and then we switch to another. <br><br>For instance, there is a major problem in the plot and the reader is completely for one side and then BOOM! POV switch and suddenly your on the other side. The whole book pushes and pulls the reader back and forth. And that's what I loved about it. It was so unique so moving and so full of joy and sorrow.<br><br>Of course, it's this aspect that would be nearly impossible to make into a movie. Not that it can't be done. It would just be hard but so would love to see someone try.<br><br>Bottom Line:<br>5 "Wow that was better than We Were Liars" Stars<br>Age Recommendation: 14+ (Sex, Kissing, Abortion, Violence, Heavy Themes)<br>For fans of: <i>We Were Liars</i>or<i>Big Little Lies</i><br><br> <br>| <a href="https://Goodreads.com/tuckeralmengor" rel="nofollow noopener">Goodreads</a> | <a href="https://tuckerthereader.wordpress.com" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://Pinterest.com/tuckeralmengor" rel="nofollow noopener">Pinterest</a> | <a href="https://linkedin.com/in/tuckeralmengor" rel="nofollow noopener">LinkedIn</a> | <a href="https://www.youtube.com/channel/UC1JLAbHwaeQ5YwayF3UhjWw" rel="nofollow noopener">YouTube</a> | <a href="https://instagram.com/tuckeralmengor" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a><br></span>
  <a data-text-id="5344905977372910344" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('HGleIpuhcIA909Hb0WYGxx4Ake4v40Un0zN80D1ViOo70ODwQMmcOHy9kRjLQBse9sYAx8PUAQkX/ZTvOQR8BQ==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('nyvDvXT2b3fjt/gFIrZsqcOAo6SD30qKz75+tZ0forK4kn1vr56Dz6LZuMY4kHFwK0YyjW/oDqQLcJaKmU5WXQ==')})
  }
//]]>
</script>

In the summer she stewed herbs for her mother, a midwife and healer, and in the winter she salvaged in her father\'s junkyard.\n\nHer father forbade hospitals, so Tara never saw a doctor or nurse. Gashes and concussions, even burns from explosions, were all treated at home with herbalism. The family was so isolated from mainstream society that there was no one to ensure the children received an education and no one to intervene when one of Tara\'s older brothers became violent.\n\nThen, lacking any formal education, Tara began to educate herself. She taught herself enough mathematics and grammar to be admitted to Brigham Young University, where she studied history, learning for the first time about important world events like the Holocaust and the civil rights movement. Her quest for knowledge transformed her, taking her over oceans and across continents, to Harvard and to Cambridge. Only then would she wonder if she\'d traveled too far, if there was still a way home.\n\nEducated is an account of the struggle for self-invention. It is a tale of fierce family loyalty and of the grief that comes with severing the closest of ties. <div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer6583471527964351994">Celeste Ng is the author of the novel Everything I Never Told You, which was a New York Times bestseller, a New York Times Notable Book of 2014, Amazon’s #1 Best Book of 2014, and named a best book of the year by over a dozen publications. Everything I Never Told You was also the winner of the Massachusetts Book Award, the Asian/Pacific American Award for Literature, the ALA’s Alex Award, and the </span>
  <span id="freeText6583471527964351994" style="display:none">Celeste Ng is the author of the novel Everything I Never Told You, which was a New York Times bestseller, a New York Times Notable Book of 2014, Amazon’s #1 Best Book of 2014, and named a best book of the year by over a dozen publications. Everything I Never Told You was also the winner of the Massachusetts Book Award, the Asian/Pacific American Award for Literature, the ALA’s Alex Award, and the Medici Book Club Prize, and was a finalist for numerous awards, including the Ohioana Award, the John Creasey (New Blood) Dagger Award, and the VCU Cabell First Novelist Award.<br /><br />Celeste grew up in Pittsburgh, Pennsylvania, and Shaker Heights, Ohio, in a family of scientists. Celeste attended Harvard University and earned an MFA from the University of Michigan (now the Helen Zell Writers’ Program at the University of Michigan), where she won the Hopwood Award. Her fiction and essays have appeared in One Story, TriQuarterly, Bellevue Literary Review, the Kenyon Review Online, and elsewhere, and she is a recipient of the Pushcart Prize.<br /><br />Currently, she lives in Cambridge, Massachusetts. Her second novel, Little Fires Everywhere, will be published by Penguin Press in fall 2017.</span>
